After all, that is the beauty of music, right? The lyrics obviously had a lot of thought and sophistication put into them, which is not what you really see in much of today's mainstream garbage. It is a must, no questions asked. 1439102430|5.0|Temperance Brennan is called out on an unusual (even for her) assignment by the coroner of the Quebec police department. As the official forensic anthropologist to the Province of Quebec, Dr. Brennan is tasked with determining the identity and cause of death of bodies that are otherwise unidentifiable. In her career in both the French-speaking province of Quebec and her American base in North Carolina, she has had to wade through swamps, dig through chemical-filled toxic waste barrels, unearth bodies from landfills and roadside graves, and sift through plane wrecks. If you've followed Tempe's colorful career, you've become inured to the gruesome details of her profession. Whether the bodies are mummified, burned beyond recognition, or unearthed after so long a time they are beyond the standard means of available to local authorities, Tempe is able to piece together the elusive clues that the dead have to reveal of who they were, how they died, and often discovering the killer's identity.<br /><br />In BONES ARE FOREVER, Tempe is summoned to a tenement apartment recently occupied by Amy Roberts, who had shown up at a hospital emergency room bleeding heavily following the apparent birth of a baby. She slipped out of the emergency room, which led to summoning the police, who suspected foul play. They searched her empty apartment looking for her or a newborn, but the only evidence they found were bloody towels in a dumpster behind the building. No woman. And no baby.<br /><br />Tempe finds not one but three tiny corpses tenderly wrapped in towels hidden behind walls in the apartment. An investigation leads to evidence that Amy, who has several aliases, is a Native American prostitute who may have fled to Yellowknife in the Northwest Territories. This leads to involvement by the Royal Canadian Mounted Police as Tempe and her former flame, Quebec homicide detective Andrew Ryan, head into the Canadian wilds. Ryan's RCMP counterpart, Sergeant Ollie Ryan, turns out to have had a brief acquaintance with Tempe, much to the embarrassment of all three, which leads to a very testy trio who must travel together deep into the Canadian interior to track down the elusive mother and possible murderer of her newborn babies.<br /><br />They uncover a much more sinister situation in Yellowknife, a rough outpost at the beginning of the infamous Ice Road. Amy's disappearance and the infant deaths are linked through a criminal connection in the growing diamond trade in the frozen wastelands. When Tempe identifies the genes of the deceased infants, she discovers that their iindigenous genes put their mother and her sisters in jeopardy.<br /><br />Tempe's trademark attention to detail delivers fascinating insight into a little known or understood connection between diamond mining and the cruel price paid by the men and women who work for the mining companies. The local residents who originally worked the played-out gold mines are dependent on the developing diamond mining industry. The destruction of the natural wildlife habitat surrounding the vast surface pits being bored into the earth in search of the world's most coveted gems is attracting another element to the region: organized crime.<br /><br />If you are a follower of the obsessive-compulsive television version of Tempe Brennan and her marriage to her FBI husband, and the book version of the single, independent woman whose love affairs often complicate her life, you will recognize the complexity of keeping the two heroines straight. These two women with the same name and profession couldn't be more different, yet Kathy Reichs remains thoroughly involved in both the screenwriting and her bestselling novels. In real life, Reichs is just as complex and brilliant as her characters, as she knows this rare profession as a veteran practitioner. It is her attention to detail and many years of  rich personal experience that lend authenticity to the details in each of her endeavors.<br /><br />Fans relish the explicit forensic minutiae and often, as in the case of BONES ARE FOREVER, receive the bonus of a comprehensive and fascinating background on diamonds, their creation and the complexities of extracting them from the earth. For some, it may lead to questioning the real worth of the tiny sparkling gem that stands for love and devotion, but is derived at a larger cost in human lives and environmental destruction.<br /><br />Reviewed by Roz Shea

B008KGPEQG|5.0|The winter of 2010-2011 delivered more than five feet of snow and a host of other meteorological insults to New York City. It's not surprising that the enforced confinement brought on by that onslaught put Paul Auster in a reflective mood on the eve of his 64th birthday. The result is WINTER JOURNAL, an idiosyncratic memoir that is at times cerebral, at times bawdy, and in every sense consistently rewarding, from a man who has spent his life \\"bleeding words onto a page.\\"<br /><br />Auster's selection of his narrative voice seems risky at first, but it's one that ultimately enhances the uncanny power of the book. He presents his reminiscences in the second person, and while we understand he's describing people and experiences that have shaped his life, it's impossible, especially for a reader anywhere close to Auster's age, to resist the subtle invitation to engage in similar excavations of memory. That sense of identification wells up from the book's first paragraph:<br /><br />\\"You think it will never happen to you, that it cannot happen to you, that you are the only person in the world to whom none of these things will ever happen, and then, one by one, they all begin to happen to you, in the same way they happen to everyone else.\\"<br /><br />From there, the story proceeds in an episodic, impressionistic fashion, true to its title as the record of the author's musings through one bleak winter. Auster is an inveterate listmaker of everything from his scars (\\"you understand that they are marks of life, that the assorted jagged lines etched into the skin of your face are letters from the secret alphabet that tells the story of who you are\\"), to his brushes with \\"a number of potentially absurd, nonsensical deaths,\\" to the 21 residences he's occupied from his birth in East Orange, New Jersey in 1947 to his current home in a four-story brownstone he shares with his wife, the writer Siri Hustvedt, in Park Slope, Brooklyn.<br /><br />That catalog of domesticity consumes some 54 of the book's 230 pages, but it's far from tedious, instead allowing Auster to discourse on subjects as diverse as his encounter with French anti-Semitism, the erratic course of his romantic life, and the birth of his writing career. Whether (as seems likely) he kept a meticulous record of these events, or merely possesses a prodigious memory, his stories overflow with precise, closely-observed detail, delivered in seductive prose whose tone ranges from darkly comic to frankly grim.<br /><br />Despite that near-perfect recall, Auster recognizes the constraints imposed on even the most acute narrator when recounting the story of one's life: \\"Some memories are so strange to you, so unlikely, so outside the realm of the plausible, that you find it difficult to reconcile them with the fact that you are the person who experienced the events you are remembering.\\"<br /><br />He devotes considerable attention to his annus horribilis of 2002, what he calls his \\"year of grim surprises.\\" In those 12 months his mother died suddenly, an event that brought forth no tears, but rather a panic attack where he recalls that \\"you lay on the floor and howled, howled at the top of your lungs, howled because death was inside you and you didn't want to die.\\" He suffered a blood clot in his leg and a damaged cornea, and caused a car accident that nearly killed his wife. Death in all its forms hovers over these events, a persistent, uninvited guest.<br /><br />Perhaps it's his recognition of how close he came to losing her that prompts his tender tribute to Hustvedt, his wife of 30 years. Whether it's his affinity for the quaint Christmas customs of her Minnesota-resident Norwegian family (\\"food as ritual, as continuity, as family cohesion --- a symbolic anchor to prevent you from drifting out to sea\\") or his description of her as \\"a brilliant woman, one of the best minds you had ever met,\\" Auster candidly acknowledges the good fortune that brought them together: \\"You didn't deserve it, but neither did you not deserve it. It just happened, and nothing can account for what happened to you except luck.\\"<br /><br />As this review is being written, amid the dog days of August, it requires a determined act of imagination to conjure up the feeling of the icy winds that will blow a few short months from now. Whether you experience what Auster calls the \\"journey through winter\\" literally or figuratively, this book will serve as a worthy companion when you embark on it.<br /><br />Reviewed by Harvey Freedenberg

B006BAEQB2|5.0|Eight-year-old Anne and her 13-year-old sister, Isabel, know from an early age that their father, Richard Neville, Earl of Warwick, is a force to be reckoned with. Denied male heirs of his own, he doesn't hesitate to use both of his daughters, the richest heiresses in England, as pawns in his high-stakes political chess games to further his own ambitions. As one of the most powerful and important men in 15th-century England, Warwick becomes widely known for his ability to maneuver his choice of leader onto the throne no matter what it takes. So skilled is he that he soon earns the nickname \\"the Kingmaker.\\"<br /><br />THE KINGMAKER'S DAUGHTER opens in 1465 with Anne, Isabel and their parents in attendance at the court of Edward IV and his queen, Elizabeth Woodville, in the Tower of London. Anne finds herself fascinated with Elizabeth, in spite of the fact that she is disliked far and wide. Considered an upstart, she is a widow and the first commoner to marry a King of England. At the time, Anne has no idea how great a role she will play in her life.<br /><br />Ever plotting to turn the tide of events in his favor, the Earl of Warwick arranges a marriage for Isabel solely with an eye to his political future. When that union doesn't turn out to be the advantage he thought it would be, he turns to Anne and marries her off to Edward, Prince of Wales. Edward is the son of Margaret of Anjou, one of the Earl's oldest enemies with whom he then decides to join forces.<br /><br />Powerless to refuse her father's orders, Anne finds herself wed to a man she barely knows and certainly doesn't love. When her father and husband are both killed only a few months into the marriage, Anne finds herself in the care of Isabel and her husband. Unfortunately, trading her father's supervision for that of her brother-in-law and sister is highly unsatisfactory to Anne.<br /><br />When Anne's childhood friend, Richard, Duke of Gloucester, approaches her, offers her his protection and declareshis love, she is only too glad to ally herself with him to free herself of the restrictions she has suffered. Luckily, this is a love match, and Anne and Richard find themselves ecstatically happy in spite of the political intrigue that swirls around them at all times.<br /><br />As time passes, however, the intrigue and scheming that take place at the royal court serve to bring a dark cloud over Anne, Isabel and their husbands. Protecting herself, her husband and her family from Elizabeth and her conspirators are the most important things to Anne, but when no one is to be trusted and spies are everywhere, it's hard to chart a course of action. Will Anne succeed in achieving her father's highest ambitions and become Queen of England, or will she be cast out into obscurity and disgrace as have so many others before her?<br /><br />THE KINGMAKER'S DAUGHTER is a fascinating account of political intrigue in England at the time of the War of the Roses. This tale of the kings of the House of York is spellbinding, riveting and oftentimes tragic. As usual, Philippa Gregory immerses us in another time and place filled with brilliant historical detail and draws us into the rich threads that make up the tapestry of human relationships as only she can.<br /><br />Reviewed by Amie Taylor

B008QDCZJ2|2.0|As a prelude to this review it must be known that I am and have been a steadfast and stalwart defender of Neil and Chris for most of my life. I am a lifelong fan and still consider them to be my favorite musical act. In my opinion they are without a doubt among the musical geniuses of our time, which makes their latest offering unfathomably perplexing and makes writing this review so painful.<br /><br />Having said that, Elysium is cold, soulless and dreadful. It's almost as if they folded over their usual biting cynicism and it became this recursive poison that spilled all over their usually sharp sense of taste. What we're left with is a bland insincere yawning stab at kludging together some leftover tracks.<br /><br />Much ado was made about working with producer Andrew Dawson, supposedly bringing a hip-hop edge to the proceedings. Well, that has been a disaster. Most of the tracks are flaccid pre-set sounding exercises in futility. Although some of the characteristic PSB sheen is there, the music is defined by a soft, turgid apologetic sound. I've heard demo-tracks on sound modules with more immediacy and grace.<br /><br />The first three tracks; Leaving, Invisible, and Winner are in part redeemable. They have that patented PSB sincerity, they live in that vast world full saudaude and possibilities that Neil is so expert in conjuring. But there is some ineffable element that has been excluded that fails to push them over the top. Mainly because they feel like echoes in exercises of previous efforts. To a neophyte that may not be obvious, but the comparisons are rich with allusions and as whole they fail to deliver the glorious cresting glory or the lush ennui of surrender of their antecedents.  They would be perfectly acceptable middle of the road tracks on a more filled out album like Nightlife or Yes, but as the high watermarks of this album they leave the whole effort a fetid swampy brackish mess.<br /><br />From there it goes downhill fast. 'Your Earlier Stuff' is ( I'm sure ) a comment on a frequent refrain, but simply comes across as snide and bitter. The sharp delightful commentary of 'Yesterday When I Was Mad' has devolved into a self indulgent sad sniping refrain completely lacking in grace or wit.<br /><br />Who was the engineer on 'A Face like That'? Muddy, Saturated, Narrow, Sharp. Should have checked it on the NS-10's No comment on the song itself.<br /><br />Breathing Space is a nice open ended track with some vague sentiments nothing to indict but also nothing to recommend.<br /><br />Ego music is an unholy amalgamation of Hit Music and Shameless phoned in from behind a veneer of self control. Shade-by-numbers. Someone needs to go back to work on that algorithm.<br /><br />Hold On is a hollow appeal from a dusty community theatre stage production of Jesus Christ superstar... and not in a good way.<br /><br />Give it a Go is the pumping chorus from the same production, sung as the cast does a 'train' chorus line while smiling garishly,  the lyrics lovingly crafted by the ambitious stage manager.<br /><br />Memory of the Future is almost there... clever concept, soaring movements, excellent arrangement, BUT. The plodding exhausted beat makes it fall on its face.  The production that so far has sat silently in the background trying it's best but not delivering has timidly stepped forward with it's awkward undulating grimace and foiled what could've been a standout track.<br /><br />Everything Means Something. Sing-songy plodding, dissonant and all that that implies.<br /><br />Requiem in Denim and Leopardskin. Finally a nearly perfect PSB track. Reminiscent of the mid-tempo swagger of Bilingual, this track delivers on all fronts. A heartfelt paen to a favorite aunt, replete with subtle references to people, places and themes that are entwined deep in the PSB DNA. It carries itself with the easy confidence of those who know, and gently expresses a respectfully playful view of thanatos with a firm conviction. A masterwork. Everything about this track, from the swaying calypso rhythms to the actual motorcycle redeems the boys in the end.<br /><br />I'm not sure how or why this album came about, I am disappointed in it as a whole, but do think that there are a few moments of brilliance. As someone who possesses every PSB releas this one will stay in its wrapping next to the others hoping that the next one will get ruined from being played too much.

Clearing each level (puzzle), revolves around your (cheaply made) creation surviving whatever test the game throws at you. The less money you spend to create whatever the level requires, the higher your star rating becomes.<br />Getting one star on all levels is very simple, and since the game has only eleven real levels... Well, it will take you about three to four hours (I'm being generous here).<br /><br />Since I downloaded the game, I already cleared all the provided levels with a one or two star rating (three stars on the first few puzzles).<br />Getting a three star rating really does require some very creative thinking, and I still can't quite figure out how to do this for most levels.<br /><br />Once you are done with the game, you can still play around in a pretty great physics based environment, with some level based surprises. I don't want to give too much away, because it really is quite fun. But you can basically mess around with your creations by blowing things up, pulling stuff apart, using slow motion, and a lot of other options. You can even zoom in and out, which is quite handy.<br />I actually spent a while just messing around on the \\"Staircase\\" level with a crash test dummy and slinky.<br /><br />This brings us to the game's excellent graphics. While most of your time will be spent in the (almost completely) blue \\"build\\" mode, or in the red and green \\"structure\\" view, when you do eventually swap to the \\"standard\\" view - the visuals will impress.<br /><br />While the game really is too short (unless you are going for a three star rating on all levels), it does have a lot of replayability by allowing you to solve each level in countless ways, and giving you a sandbox environment to toy around with.<br /><br />However, this app is not without its share of problems.<br /><br />My main issue with the gameis its pushy in game advertising.<br />Starting up SimplePhysics sometimes results in the following message: \\"I'm working on new games for physics minded people. Would you like me to send you an e-mail when I release a new game?\\"<br />Your choices are Yes and No. Selecting No clears the message for the time being, but for some reason does not disable it. I still had it pop up multiple times during my many play sessions. This needs to stop. No should mean NO.<br />There is another message, that actually appears during gameplay! It states: \\"Are you hungry for new physics & engineering puzzles? Check out my newest game, Dummy Defense! It has 57 levels of brain bending puzzles that only the smartest will conquer.\\", and just like with the previous message, declining it results in the darn thing coming back after a few games.<br />While not constant, these things are still annoying and bothersome in an otherwise good game.<br />------------ EDIT START HERE---------<br />The developer has informed me that this is a bug, and these things should only pop up once. Once that is fixed, my opinion of the game will be even higher.<br />------------ EDIT END HERE---------<br /><br />Another issue I have is the inclusion of network permissions. All of these options can be conveniently reached from the main menu.<br />While the game does also allow you to send your blueprints to a friend, this is done through a separate e-mail client and does not require the game to have full network permissions.<br /><br />Yet another concern is the fact that there are absolutely no sound or music effects in the game, at all. Nothing you do will make any noise. Eventually one gets used to the quite, but at least some sound would help out.<br /><br />My final problem with the game are all the fake five star reviews from single review posters. Developers need to learn that payingsomeone (or using a dummy account) for this purpose is not the best idea. These reviews are easy to spot and actually do more harm than good.<br /><br />To sum things up, I want to say that overall I am very pleased with this game. While short in itself, the sandbox feature adds quite a bit of replay value, and the price is fair.<br />Go ahead and download this as todays FAOTD, or buy it for the $.99 that Jundroo, LLC wants for it.

B0038QGXHW|3.0|I have to admit that my review appears to be contrary to the popular view of this release by Keith Jarrett and Charlie Haden. I think I appreciate a different aesthetic when it comes to jazz, especially piano jazz, and most especially piano jazz by Keith Jarrett. In the liner notes of this CD, Jarrett says that \\"I wanted only the distilled essence of what we had, and it took some time to wean ourselves from going for hip solos or unevenly played tunes (even though they had wonderful things inside them.\\"<br /><br />My chief problem with this CD is that I am actually LOOKING for hip solos and for unevently played tunes with wonderful things inside them, because to me, that is the essence of jazz: taking chances and going for broke, NOT artificially restraining oneself in order to play ONLY the \\"essence\\" of the tune. The result of all too much restraint is boring, non-adventurous performances that don't stray far from the straight-ahead melody. If I just wanted to hear the melody and very slight departures from the melody, I would listen to non-jazz performances of them.<br /><br />There are simply very few sparks of genius or breathtaking melodic adventures here. For the most part, any competent journeyman jazz player could replicate these performances without breaking a sweat. Maybe I'm missing something here, but that's the way I feel.<br /><br />There are notable departures from this formula: Body and Soul is a gorgeous, sustained journey into reharmonization and near-recomposition, and I enjoy this performance immensely.<br /><br />Perhaps this release is most enjoyable late at night, when up-tempo, dizzying improvisations can come across as too much. This is romantic ear candy for late night listening. Enjoy it as such, and you won't be disappointed.

B004AOECUG|5.0|Legend has it that Martin Scorsese intended \\"Raging Bull\\" (1980) as the last movie he would ever make.<br /><br />Still reeling from the box-office disappointment of \\"New York, New York\\" (1977), recovering from his drug addictions and witnessing American cinema's transition from the 1970s New Hollywood period into the modern blockbuster era, Scorsese mustered all his energy, all his strength, all his cinematic knowledge to create a movie that was so raw, so uncompromising that any suggestion that the movie would achieve box-office glory was out of the question. \\"Raging Bull\\" was meant to be culmination of Martin Scorsese's undisputed talents as a filmmaker and his last attempt to be heard among American moviegoers. Thankfully, the latter was not the case as Scorsese continued to make more movies but \\"Raging Bull\\" undeniably stands as his magnum opus. Even though \\"Taxi Driver\\" and \\"GoodFellas\\" were more popular movies, it's safe to say no other Martin Scorsese movie (or few movies in general) was as powerful, devastating and hard to watch as \\"Raging Bull\\".<br /><br />Like many of the great gangster movies of the 30s-60s, \\"Raging Bull\\" depicts the rise and turbulent fall of a flawed hero but hero is used in a very loose sense here. The hero in \\"Raging Bull\\", middleweight boxer Jake La Motta, is a despicable, ignorant and antisocial brute whose overbearing machismo, violent behavior and sexual insecurity made him a menace inside and outside the ring. No one was safe from La Motta's wrath, not his opponents, his brother, his wife or even himself. \\"Raging Bull\\" unflinchingly depicts the spectacular fall of Jake La Motta as he goes from a dangerous success story in the ring to a miserable failure as a brother, husband and a man.<br /><br />Robert De Niro's Oscar-winning performance as La Motta is one of the greatest achievements in acting history: De Niro invests every raw emotion into his character, revealing La Motta to be as a self-destructive and insecure human being who sees violence as the answer to everything. Rather he tells his brother Joe to punch him for having \\"girly hands\\", tormenting his wife when he senses her cheating, beating up guys so that they're \\"not pretty anymore\\" or hitting the wall in self-hatred when he reaches the lowest moment of his life, De Niro ignites the screen with the fury of a raging boxer. It's easy to mock the fact that De Niro gained 30-50 pounds to play La Motta in his later years but it's no publicity stunt; the emotional and physical weight that De Niro bestows on his character reveals a raging bull that cannot be tamed.<br /><br />Besides De Niro, the other performances in \\"Raging Bull\\" are absolutely superlative including Cathy Moriarty as De Niro's wife Vicki and Joe Pesci as Jake's manager brother Joe. One of the most memorable scenes in \\"Raging Bull\\" is not the brutal boxing scenes but set in a living room where Jake suspiciously believes that Joe is having an affair with his wife Vicki. In the midst of verbal fisticuffs (\\"Did you f--- my wife?\\"), it is the way De Niro shows the inner twisting logic of his jealousy that speaks volumes.<br /><br />Besides the magnificent acting, the movie represents a cinematic peak for Scorsese and his crew. By shooting the film in black and white, Scorsese gave the picture a gritty, unrefined style that combined elements of film noir with the rawness of John Cassavetes movies; the Bronx has never looked hotter and more dangerous. Thelma Schoonmaker's editing and Michael Champman's cinematography are absolutely outstanding, particularly in the fights between Sugar Ray Robinson and La Motta where they make those scenes look savage and poetic through slow motion, off-kilter camera angles and rapid edits. To make the boxing scenes more grisly, the crew even made use of animal sound effects!<br /><br />\\"Raging Bull\\" was voted by several critics as the best movie of the 1980s. For once, the superlatives do not lie. \\"Raging Bull\\" is an encompassing masterpiece that does not date but grows through the passage of time. \\"GoodFellas\\", \\"Casino\\" and \\"The Departed\\" are outstanding movies but for my money, no one involved in this great movie (not even Scorsese) has done better work since. This movie is more than a classic; it's an imperishable work of art.<br /><br />Strongest recommendation to buy at all costse that does not date but grows through the passage of time. \\"GoodFellas\\", \\"Casino\\" and \\"The Departed\\" are outstanding movies but for my money, no one involved in this great movie (not even Scorsese) has done better work since. This movie is more than a classic; it's an imperishable work of art.<br /><br />Strongest recommendation to buy at all costs

B000002U82|5.0|One of the most successful rock albums of all time, selling 50 million copies worldwide and staying on the Billboard 200 charts for an extraordinary 741 weeks between 1973 to 1988. But to judge \\"Dark Side\\" solely on its commercial success is to overlook the artistic merits that the album possesses. Time has done nothing but burnish the brilliance of Pink Floyd's magnum opus, their major breakthrough into the US mainstream and an album that has justly earned its place as one of the greatest rock albums ever made.<br /><br />Pink Floyd are a progressive rock band that even people that hate progressive rock bands love. It's easy to see why: many progressive rock bands like Genesis, Emerson, Lake & Palmer, Rush, Yes, Procol Harum and the Moody Blues made music that was too excessive for anyone's taste, creating records that were long-winded, pretentious and often mistaking bombast for majesty (And indeed, is there anything more bombastic than a band releasing three one-sided solo albums under its own name, as ELP did with \\"Works\\"?). Pink Floyd's music was long, meticulous and epic as well but it possessed a strong simple musicality that made Floyd's music a pleasure to listen to, even for fans that disdained space rock. It also helped that they had one of the greatest songwriters of all time in Roger Waters, the band's bassist. In short, they made meticulously detailed music that was filled with emotion, intellect and melody.<br /><br />\\"Dark Side\\", which was their eighth studio album, crystallizes that attitude more than anything. In all the nine songs of \\"Dark Side\\", Roger Waters, along with guitarist David Gilmour, keyboardist Richard Wright and drummer Nick Mason, evoked big, universal landscapes of human crises, governmental incompetence and mundane everyday living, tackling themes such as conflict, consumerism, passage of time, fear of death, madness and the follies of war. The concepts are simple enough but given the backdrop of atmospheric soundspaces, creative sound effects and elements of blues, jazz and art-rock thrown in for good measure, the album as a whole becomes transcendent.<br /><br />Each of the nine songs is a classic in itself but the best and appropriate way to enjoy the album is to listen to it from beginning to end, the way it was intended. It may seem like a chore but on an absorbing album like \\"Dark Side\\", such complaints hardly matter since the music is great. It is still a revelation to hear how the first side begins with the subtle sound collage of \\"Speak to Me\\" and then transiting into the leisurely paced sigh of \\"Breathe\\" before fading into the aural frenzy of \\"On the Run\\" and then into the neo-psychedelic rocker \\"Time\\" and finally the soulful piano-based instrumental \\"The Great Gig in the Sky\\", the latter featuring a chilling vocal performance by Claire Torry. Side two follows suit starting with the blues-rock classic \\"Money\\", then fading into the somber jazz-fused \\"Us and Them\\", the trippy psychedelia of \\"Any Colour You Like\\" and concluding with the double whopper in \\"Brain Damage\\" and \\"Eclipse\\". Some of these songs, particularly \\"Time\\", \\"Money\\" and \\"Us and Them\\" are classic singles but listening to the whole album is more essential since it achieves greater emotional resonance and lure listeners into a dark, haunting world of feeble human conditions.<br /><br />The production in \\"Dark Side\\" is just extraordinary. After all, there's a reason why \\"Dark Side\\" is regarded as one of the best-produced rock albums ever made. Check out \\"Money\\", which begins with the clattering of cash registers before one of the most recognizable basslines is played and the band goes into a blues frenzy featuring a great saxophone solo by Dick Parry and a rip-roaring guitar solo by David Gilmour. Similarly, \\"Time\\" begins with a long introductory passage of clocks chirming and alarms ringing, followed by a two-minute drum solo from Mason and then a neo-psychedelic workout containing Gilmour singing the verses and RichardWright singing the bridge about how time slips by. Each song possesses a strong identity that makes one distinctive from another and the combination of Waters' poetic lyrics and awesome production make this a gripping listen for even those that hate prog rock. That this album came out at a time before digital technology and Pro Tools became a norm makes it even more relevant today than it did back in '73.<br /><br />Pink Floyd was a band of great talent and ambition but it was also a band that had many naysayers. Many rock critics, particularly those in the late 1970s, slammed Pink Floyd as the apotheosis of stale, boring dinosaur rock music while praising punk rock albums like the Sex Pistols' \\"Never Mind the Bullocks, Here's the Sex Pistols\\", the Vibrators' \\"Pure Mania\\" and the Damned's \\"Damned Damned Damned\\". Oddly enough, though, it is THOSE albums - not \\"Dark Side\\" - which sound dated today.<br /><br />Such charges that Pink Floyd were a boring, dinosaur act are understandable in the light of the late 1980s when Floyd reformed and released four terrible albums (two studio, two live) that earned a lot of money but created the false impression that they were a glorified oldies band. But in the 1970s, Pink Floyd were one of the best and most intelligent rock bands of all time. Every album they made in the 70's - \\"Meddle\\", \\"Dark Side\\", \\"Wish You Were Here\\", \\"Animals\\" and \\"The Wall\\", as well as underrated gems like \\"Obscured by Clouds\\" and the second side of \\"Atom Heart Mother\\" - were powerful parables of everyday life, told with fearsome intellect and crafted with melodic precision, atmospheric aura and emotional power. Their music is far more timeless and modern than Johnny Rotten whining about the state of England.<br /><br />It's been joked around that \\"Dark Side of the Moon\\" is best heard when you are under the influence of drugs such as acid and pills. Sorry, but such a feeble statement does this album a great disservice. I did not need to take drugs to recognize the greatness of \\"Dark Side\\". Even as sober, I knew I had witnessed something never heard before and probably never again in the nearby future. \\"Dark Side\\" is that lightning-in-the-bottle CD where four talented musicians got together and created an imperishable work of art that will endure, no matter how many musical changes occur, how many trends are set or how many decades have gone by.<br /><br />\\"Dark Side\\" deservedly earns its place as one of the all-time great rock albums. Simply put, if you don't have this album in your CD collection, don't bother to have one.<br /><br />Strongest recommendation to buy at all costs.Wright singing the bridge about how time slips by. If you find this to be the case, stick with it. Before this you had only done it along one string....easy-peasy.  From here on out you've got to have your thinking cap on .......and you're only on page 23. I think an argument for hybrid learning can be inserted here, because my feeling is that some sections of the workbook might stop the less-persisent in their tracks.  Trying to figure out those major scale patterns and patching them together up and down the fretboard could be one of those sections.  That ones a biggy. 0525953728|3.0|No Easy Day: The Firsthand Account of the Mission That Killed Osama Bin Laden by Mark Owen and Kevin Maurer<br /><br />Before I start with the formal review, let me state that my goal for all my reviews is to provide fellow readers with an honest assessment of the quality of the book. It has nothing to do with my feelings about whether the author should have written the book or not. I have the utmost respect and admiration for these young heroes. I am in awe of what they do and I thank them from the bottom of my heart for all the great sacrifices that they make for the sake of our country. The best to \\"Mark Owen\\" and the SEAL family. Now back to the review.<br /><br />\\"No Easy Day: The Firsthand Account of the Mission That Killed Osama Bin Laden\\" is the cautious firsthand SEAL's account of one of the most newsworthy missions ever. Ex-Navy Seal and member of elite SEAL Team Six \\"Mark Owen\\" provides the reader with a personal and firsthand account of what actually happened on the night of his most noteworthy mission and other interesting assignments that occurred during his career as a SEAL from 1998 to 2012. This 336-page book is composed of nineteen chapters but is in essence can be broken out into two halves: the first half, is about his training and his development as a SEAL and all his assignments not including the night that led to Bin Laden's death; the second half is strictly about the main mission and what turned out to be the most interesting part of this book. What hurts this otherwise fascinating and mesmerizing topic is the lack of details that most likely were kept out because of legal considerations. The quality of the book suffered as a result of it.<br /><br />Positives:<br />1. As fascinating a topic as you will ever find.<br />2. Well-written and provides an inside look into the courageous world of a Navy SEAL at a very accessible level.<br />3. The author has a humble sense of honor that permeates the book.<br />4. What it takes to be a SEAL Team Six/DEVGRU member. The training, the mental toughness, the courage and the missions associated with such an elite team.<br />5. The brief history of SEAL Team Six.<br />6. The first half the book covers the author's training and those missions prior to the mission at Abbottabad. He goes into some details of the main missions he was involved with and the role he played for that assigned mission.<br />7. The weaponry, the gadgets...I wanted more!<br />8. Interesting look at collaboration between teams and outside resources.<br />9. At times, you feel you are right in the middle of the action. The author captures some of the adrenaline rush that happens during a mission and most importantly how the element of surprise and the unexpected plays out. \\"One of the key lessons learned early on in a SEAL's career was the ability to be comfortable being uncomfortable\\".<br />10. The mission to save the Maersk Alabama's captain Richard Phillips was a very interesting one and illustrates many of the variables involved with such a mission.<br />11. I enjoy SEAL jargon and all their running jokes. For instance \\"pax\\" are people,<br />12. Interesting though limited insight into the logistics involved with the missions.<br />13. The practical difficulties that SEALS encounter including having to deal with some restrictive policies. The failed missions or missions that did not meet their ultimate objectives...<br />14. The second half of the book, basically from chapter 9 on is where the book really takes off. This of course, deals with the mission to get Bin Laden or as referred to, UBL.<br />15. The inside scoop, from the pre-planning, the mission and the return home including a visit with the President. This is by far the best part of the book and the author succeeds in giving you a firsthand account on what really happened.<br />16. A brief history of the formation of Al Qaeda.<br />17. A surprise element (I won't spoil it) that ties the beginning of the book with the visit to meetthe President.<br />18. What happened to the author a year after the Bin Laden mission or Operation Neptune Spear if you must.<br />19. A confirming sources/Bibliography section.<br /><br />Negatives:<br />1. No doubt about it, the author was restricted and perhaps in the bigger picture rightfully so but it obviously hurt the overall quality of the book. He goes to great pains to tell the reader that he has protected tactics, techniques and procedures and that if you are looking for secrets this is not your book.<br />2. A book intended for the masses as this was, merited an appendix that included pictures, specifications of all the weaponry and large assets. There is a brief photo insert but not enough to do the book justice. I understand some of its confidential but certainly there is enough unclassified information that could have been shared and would have added value to the book.<br />3. The second half of the book is vastly more interesting than the first half and saves this book from being generic.<br />4. Very little on family life and the obvious difficulties in being able to maintain a marriage. Once again, it may have something to do with protecting the identities.<br />5. I hate to say it but there are better books on this very topic. Look at my further suggestions for books on this and related topics.<br />6. There wasn't any major surprises in the book. Much of what was here I have either read or saw on the news.<br /><br />In summary, reservations aside I still enjoyed the book. The looming legal restrictions diluted what could have been a much better book and quite frankly there are much better books out there but there is something to be said for a personal account of what happened. It's my contention that the layperson will enjoy this book more than the more avid reader of this genre. Be that as it may, the fascinating firsthand account of the Abbottabad mission that ended Bin Laden's life is what makes this book worthwhile to read.<br /><br />Further suggestions: \\"[[ASIN:0307955575 Manhunt: The Ten-Year Search for Bin Laden--from 9/11 to Abbottabad]]\\" and \\"[[ASIN:B001PO6APO Holy War, Inc.: Inside the Secret World of Osama bin Laden]]\\" by Peter L. Bergen, \\"[[ASIN:1250012198 Counterstrike: The Untold Story of America's Secret Campaign Against Al Qaeda]]\\" by Eric Schmitt and Thom Shanker, \\"[[ASIN:0691137021 The Science of War: Defense Budgeting, Military Technology, Logistics, and Combat Outcomes]]\\" by Michael E. This is truly a book that can be used and prove beneficial to those that need a boost in time management.
B005LAJ23A|5.0|------------------------------------------------------------<br />\\"The Walking Dead: The Complete Second Season\\"<br />(AMC, 2012)<br />------------------------------------------------------------<br />In its second season, the live-action adaptation of Robert Kirkman's \\"Walking Dead\\" moves from its emergence as a thrilling new show into a top-notch TV drama. Fans of the comicbook series that the show is based on simply have to let go of the original narrative - the television producers made a clear decision to depart from the strict confines of the print version. Many characters are the same, and the overall zombie-plague scenario remains, but there are many significant changes. And changes for the better, I'd have to say. The comics are great, but so is this show, and I think the move to have the TV show be its own thing is fine -- the scripts are great, the drama is riveting, and the cast are taking ownership of the characters, giving them their own voices. The show is still character-driven, more about the moral crucible of disaster and how each person deals with the tensions between communal effort and individual survival, but the horror, when we see it, is also pretty freaky and intense.<br /><br />All in all, AMC's \\"Walking Dead\\" is an unqualified success, with the second season much stronger than the first, and the third season a must-see as well. I can't wait. (DJ Joe Sixpack, Slipcue film reviews)

0817439390|5.0|I bought this book because a photography blog had mentioned what a great read it was in terms of basic photography concepts.  I have always read manuals inside and out, and have used compact digital cameras extensively.  However when I have messed around with DSLR's, I never knew what to do with the aperature or shutter priority modes.
